				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Pfizer Inc.">Pfizer Inc.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p>  
 
<span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Pfizer&amp;params=41.3343429_N_72.06795_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">41°20′04″N</span> <span class="longitude">72°04′05″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">41.3343429°N 72.06795°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">41.3343429; -72.06795</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p>
<p><b>Pfizer Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceutical">pharmaceutical</a> corporation headquartered in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. It is one of the world's largest pharmaceutical companies.<sup id="cite_ref-businessweek_2012_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek_2012-4">[4]</a></sup> It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>, and its shares have been a component of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> since 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Dow_Pfizer_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dow_Pfizer-5">[5]</a></sup> Pfizer ranked No. 57 on the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Pfizer Inc.</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="logo" style="text-align:center"><a srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$63.14 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(2019)</span><sup id="cite_ref-pfizerFR2019_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfizerFR2019-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">~88,300 (2019)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pfizer.com">Pfizer.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>On December 19, 2018, Pfizer announced a joint merger of their consumer healthcare division with UK pharma giant <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>; the British company will maintain a controlling share (listed at 68%).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>The company developed and produces medicines and vaccines for a wide range of medical disciplines, including immunology, oncology, cardiology, endocrinology, and neurology. Its products include the blockbuster drug Lipitor (<a href="/wiki/Atorvastatin" title="Atorvastatin">atorvastatin</a>), used to lower <a href="/wiki/Low-density_lipoprotein" title="Low-density lipoprotein">LDL</a> blood cholesterol; Lyrica (<a href="/wiki/Pregabalin" title="Pregabalin">pregabalin</a>) for neuropathic pain and fibromyalgia; Diflucan (<a href="/wiki/Fluconazole" title="Fluconazole">fluconazole</a>), an oral antifungal medication; Zithromax (<a href="/wiki/Azithromycin" title="Azithromycin">azithromycin</a>), an antibiotic; Viagra (<a href="/wiki/Sildenafil" title="Sildenafil">sildenafil</a>) for erectile dysfunction; and Celebrex (also Celebra, <a href="/wiki/Celecoxib" title="Celecoxib">celecoxib</a>), an anti-inflammatory drug.
</p><p>In 2016, Pfizer Inc. was expected to merge with <a href="/wiki/Allergan" title="Allergan">Allergan</a> to create the Ireland-based "Pfizer plc" in a deal that would have been worth $160 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The merger was called off in April 2016, however, because of new rules from the United States Treasury against tax inversions, a method of avoiding taxes by merging with a foreign company.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The company has made the second-largest pharmaceutical settlement with the United States Department of Justice.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlespfizer.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Charlespfizer.jpg/170px-Charlespfizer.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="190" data-file-height="246"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 220px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Charlespfizer.jpg/170px-Charlespfizer.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="220" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charlespfizer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charles Pfizer</div></div></div>
<p>In 1849, Pfizer was founded in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> by German-American <a href="/wiki/Charles_Pfizer" title="Charles Pfizer">Charles Pfizer</a> and his cousin <a href="/wiki/Charles_F._Erhart" title="Charles F. Erhart">Charles F. Erhart</a> from <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsburg" title="Ludwigsburg">Ludwigsburg</a>, Germany. They launched the chemicals business, Charles Pfizer and Company, from a building at the intersection of Harrison Avenue and Bartlett Street<sup id="cite_ref-Citycyclopedia_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citycyclopedia-10">[10]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Brooklyn" title="Williamsburg, Brooklyn">Williamsburg, Brooklyn</a>, where they produced an <a href="/wiki/Antiparasitic" title="Antiparasitic">antiparasitic</a> called <a href="/wiki/Santonin" title="Santonin">santonin</a>. This was an immediate success, although it was the production of <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid" title="Citric acid">citric acid</a> that led to Pfizer's growth in the 1880s. Pfizer continued to buy property to expand its lab and factory. Pfizer's original administrative headquarters was at 81 Maiden Lane in Manhattan.<sup id="cite_ref-Citycyclopedia_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Citycyclopedia-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>By 1906, sales totaled $3.4 million.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> caused a shortage of <a href="/wiki/Calcium_citrate" title="Calcium citrate">calcium citrate</a>, which Pfizer imported from Italy for the manufacture of citric acid, and the company began a search for an alternative supply. Pfizer chemists learned of a fungus that ferments sugar to citric acid, and they were able to commercialize production of citric acid from this source in 1919. The company developed expertise in fermentation technology as a result. These skills were applied to the mass production of the antibiotic <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">penicillin</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in response to the need to treat injured Allied soldiers; most of the penicillin that went ashore with the troops on <a href="/wiki/D-Day" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day">D-Day</a> was made by Pfizer.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-11">[11]</a></sup></p><p>Penicillin became very inexpensive in the 1940s, and Pfizer searched for new antibiotics with greater profit potential. They discovered <a href="/wiki/Oxytetracycline" title="Oxytetracycline">Terramycin (oxytetracycline)</a> in 1950, and this changed the company from a manufacturer of fine chemicals to a research-based pharmaceutical company. Pfizer developed a drug discovery program focused on in vitro synthesis in order to augment its research in fermentation technology. The company also established an animal health division in 1959 with an 700-acre (2.8 km<sup>2</sup>) farm and research facility in <a href="/wiki/Terre_Haute,_Indiana" title="Terre Haute, Indiana">Terre Haute, Indiana</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>By the 1950s, Pfizer had established offices in Belgium, Brazil, Canada, Cuba, Mexico, Panama, Puerto Rico, and the United Kingdom. In 1960, the company moved its medical research laboratory operations out of New York City to a new facility in Groton, Connecticut. In 1980, they launched <a href="/wiki/Piroxicam" title="Piroxicam">Feldene (piroxicam)</a>, a prescription anti-inflammatory medication that became Pfizer's first product to reach one billion dollars in total sales.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> During the 1980s and 1990s, Pfizer Corporation growth was sustained by the discovery and marketing of Zoloft, Lipitor, Norvasc, Zithromax, Aricept, Diflucan, and Viagra.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2000.E2.80.932010"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000–2010">2000–2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2000–2010" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In this decade, Pfizer grew by mergers, including those with <a href="/wiki/Warner%E2%80%93Lambert" title="Warner–Lambert">Warner–Lambert</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Pharmacia" title="Pharmacia">Pharmacia</a> (2003), and <a href="/wiki/Wyeth" title="Wyeth">Wyeth</a> (2009).
</p><p>In 2003, the company acquired <a href="/wiki/Esperion_Therapeutics" title="Esperion Therapeutics">Esperion Therapeutics</a> for $1.3 billion (later selling the unit in 2008), protecting Lipitor from <a href="/wiki/ETC-216" class="mw-redirect" title="ETC-216">ETC-216</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2004, Pfizer announced it would acquire Meridica for $125 million.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2005, the company acquired Vicuron Pharmaceuticals for $1.9 billion, Idun for just less than $300 million and finally Angiosyn for $527 million.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>On June 26, 2006, Pfizer announced it would sell its Consumer Healthcare unit (manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Listerine" title="Listerine">Listerine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicorette" title="Nicorette">Nicorette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visine" title="Visine">Visine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudafed" class="mw-redirect" title="Sudafed">Sudafed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neomycin/polymyxin_B/bacitracin" title="Neomycin/polymyxin B/bacitracin">Neosporin</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a> for $16.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-investor_dec_2006_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investor_dec_2006-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_dec_2006_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_dec_2006-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>Development of <a href="/wiki/Torcetrapib" title="Torcetrapib">torcetrapib</a>, a drug that increases production of <a href="/wiki/High_density_lipoprotein" class="mw-redirect" title="High density lipoprotein">HDL</a>, or "good cholesterol", which reduces <a href="/wiki/Low_density_lipoprotein" class="mw-redirect" title="Low density lipoprotein">LDL</a> thought to be correlated to heart disease, was cancelled in December 2006. During a Phase III clinical trial involving 15,000 patients, more deaths occurred in the group that took the medicine than expected, and a sixty percent increase in mortality was seen among patients taking the combination of torcetrapib and Lipitor versus Lipitor alone. Lipitor alone was not implicated in the results, but Pfizer lost nearly $1 billion developing the failed drug and the market value of the company plummeted afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_2006_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_2006-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Berenson_20061203_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berenson_20061203-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> That same year, the company also announced it would acquire PowerMed and Rivax.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In September 2009, Pfizer pleaded guilty to the illegal marketing of the arthritis drug <a href="/wiki/Valdecoxib#2009_settlement_for_off-label_uses_promotions" title="Valdecoxib">Bextra</a> for uses unapproved by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA), and agreed to a $2.3 billion settlement, the largest health care fraud settlement at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>A July 2010 article in <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">BusinessWeek</a></i> reported that Pfizer was seeing more success in its battle against makers of <a href="/wiki/Counterfeit" title="Counterfeit">counterfeit</a> prescription drugs by pursuing civil lawsuits rather than criminal prosecution. Pfizer has hired customs and narcotics experts from all over the globe to track down fakes and assemble evidence that can be used to pursue civil suits for <a href="/wiki/Trademark_infringement" title="Trademark infringement">trademark infringement</a>. Since 2007, Pfizer has spent $3.3 million on investigations and legal fees and recovered about $5.1 million, with another $5 million tied up in ongoing cases.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>On May 6, 2013, Pfizer told The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> it would begin selling Viagra directly to patients via its website.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span id="Warner.E2.80.93Lambert_acquisition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Warner–Lambert_acquisition">Warner–Lambert acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Warner–Lambert acquisition" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>Pfizer acquired <a href="/wiki/Warner%E2%80%93Lambert" title="Warner–Lambert">Warner–Lambert</a> in 2000 for $111.8 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> at the time, created the second largest pharmaceutical company in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Warner–Lambert was founded as a <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia</a> drug store in 1856 by William R. Warner. Inventing a tablet-coating process gained Warner a place in the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>. Parke–Davis was founded in <a href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan" class="mw-redirect" title="Detroit, Michigan">Detroit</a> in 1866 by Hervey Parke and George Davis. Warner–Lambert took over Parke–Davis in 1976, and acquired <a href="/wiki/Wilkinson_Sword" title="Wilkinson Sword">Wilkinson Sword</a> in 1993 and Agouron Pharmaceuticals in 1999.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacia_acquisition">Pharmacia acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pharmacia acquisition" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Pfizer merged with <a href="/wiki/Pharmacia" title="Pharmacia">Pharmacia</a>. The merger was again driven in part by the desire to acquire full rights to a product, this time Celebrex (<a href="/wiki/Celecoxib" title="Celecoxib">celecoxib</a>), the <a href="/wiki/COX-2_selective_inhibitor" class="mw-redirect" title="COX-2 selective inhibitor">COX-2 selective inhibitor</a> previously jointly marketed by <a href="/wiki/G._D._Searle_%26_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="G. D. Searle &amp; Company">Searle</a> (acquired by Pharmacia) and Pfizer. In the ensuing years, Pfizer carried out a massive restructuring that resulted in numerous site closures and the loss of jobs including <a href="/wiki/Terre_Haute,_Indiana" title="Terre Haute, Indiana">Terre Haute</a>, Indiana; <a href="/wiki/Holland,_Michigan" title="Holland, Michigan">Holland</a>, Michigan; <a href="/wiki/Groton,_Connecticut" title="Groton, Connecticut">Groton</a>, Connecticut; <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York; <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Kent" title="Sandwich, Kent">Sandwich</a>, UK; and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.
</p><p>Pharmacia had been formed by a series of mergers and acquisitions from its predecessors, including Searle, <a href="/wiki/Upjohn" title="Upjohn">Upjohn</a> and <a href="/wiki/SUGEN" title="SUGEN">SUGEN</a>.
</p><p>In April 1888, Searle was founded in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a> by Gideon Daniel Searle. In 1908, the company was incorporated in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, Illinois. In 1941, the company established headquarters in Skokie, Illinois. It was acquired by the <a href="/wiki/Monsanto_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Monsanto Company">Monsanto Company</a>, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a>, Missouri, in 1985.
</p><p>The Upjohn Company was a pharmaceutical manufacturing firm founded in 1886 in <a href="/wiki/Kalamazoo,_Michigan" title="Kalamazoo, Michigan">Kalamazoo, Michigan</a>, by Dr. <a href="/wiki/William_E._Upjohn" title="William E. Upjohn">William E. Upjohn</a>, a graduate of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> medical school. The company was originally formed to make friable pills, which were designed to be easily digested.  Greenstone was founded in 1993 by Upjohn as a generics division.<sup id="cite_ref-PT2008_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT2008-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1995, Upjohn merged with Pharmacia, to form <a href="/wiki/Pharmacia_%26_Upjohn" title="Pharmacia &amp; Upjohn">Pharmacia &amp; Upjohn</a>. Pharmacia was created in April 2000 through the merger of Pharmacia &amp; Upjohn with the Monsanto Company and its G.D. Searle unit. The merged company was based in Peapack, New Jersey. The agricultural division was spun off from Pharmacia, as Monsanto, in preparation for the close of the acquisition by Pfizer.<sup id="cite_ref-urlPharmacia_to_Spin_Off_Monsanto_Stake,_Less_Than_2_Years_After_Firms_Merger_Wall_Street_Journal_28nov01_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urlPharmacia_to_Spin_Off_Monsanto_Stake,_Less_Than_2_Years_After_Firms_Merger_Wall_Street_Journal_28nov01-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>SUGEN, a company focused on <a href="/wiki/Protein_kinase" title="Protein kinase">protein kinase</a> inhibitors, was founded in 1991 in <a href="/wiki/Redwood_City,_California" title="Redwood City, California">Redwood City, California</a>, and acquired by <a href="/wiki/Pharmacia" title="Pharmacia">Pharmacia</a> in 1999. The company pioneered the use of ATP-mimetic small molecules to block <a href="/wiki/Signal_transduction" title="Signal transduction">signal transduction</a>. After the Pfizer merger, the SUGEN site was shut down in 2003, with the loss of over 300 jobs, and several programs were transferred to Pfizer. These included <a href="/wiki/Sunitinib" title="Sunitinib">sunitinib</a> (Sutent), which was approved for human use by the FDA in January 2006, passed $1 billion in annual revenues for Pfizer in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> A related compound, SU11654 (<a href="/wiki/Toceranib" title="Toceranib">Toceranib</a>), was also approved for <a href="/wiki/Cancer_in_dogs" title="Cancer in dogs">canine tumors</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/ALK_inhibitor" title="ALK inhibitor">ALK inhibitor</a> <a href="/wiki/Crizotinib" title="Crizotinib">Crizotinib</a> also grew out of a SUGEN program.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>In 2003, the new Pfizer made Greenstone (originally established as a division of Upjohn) its generic division, and focused on selling <a href="/wiki/Authorized_generics" title="Authorized generics">authorized generics</a> of Pfizer's products.<sup id="cite_ref-PT2008_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT2008-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, Pfizer announced 275 job cuts at the Kalamazoo manufacturing facility. Kalamazoo was previously the world headquarters for the Upjohn Company.<sup id="cite_ref-urlPfizer_plant_in_Michigan_to_cut_275_-_FiercePharma_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urlPfizer_plant_in_Michigan_to_cut_275_-_FiercePharma-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Wyeth_acquisition">Wyeth acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Wyeth acquisition" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On January 26, 2009, after more than a year of talks between the two companies, Pfizer agreed to buy pharmaceuticals rival <a href="/wiki/Wyeth" title="Wyeth">Wyeth</a> for a combined US$68 billion in cash, shares and loans, including some US$22.5 billion lent by five major <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> banks. The deal cemented Pfizer's position as the largest pharmaceutical company in the world, with the merged company generating over US$20 billion in cash each year, and was the largest corporate merger since <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a> and <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a>'s US$70 billion deal in March 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The combined company was expected to save US$4 billion annually through streamlining; however, as part of the deal, both companies must repatriate billions of dollars in revenue from foreign sources to the United States, which will result in higher tax costs. The acquisition was completed on October 15, 2009, making Wyeth a wholly owned subsidiary of Pfizer.<sup id="cite_ref-PfizerWyeth_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PfizerWyeth-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>The merger was broadly criticized. <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a>'s Gary Pisano told <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a>, "the record of big mergers and acquisitions in Big Pharma has just not been good. There's just been an enormous amount of shareholder wealth destroyed."<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Analysts said at the time, "The Warner–Lambert and Pharmacia mergers do not appear to have achieved gains for shareholders, so it is unclear who benefits from the Wyeth–Pfizer merger to many critics."<sup id="cite_ref-Matthew_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="King_Pharmaceuticals_acquisition">King Pharmaceuticals acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: King Pharmaceuticals acquisition" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2010, Pfizer agreed to buy <a href="/wiki/King_Pharmaceuticals" title="King Pharmaceuticals">King Pharmaceuticals</a> for $3.6 billion in cash or $14.25 per share: an approximately 40% premium over King's closing share price October 11, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-htanna_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-htanna-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2011.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–present">2011–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2011–present" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, it was announced that Pfizer was to close its UK research and development facility (formerly also a manufacturing plant) in <a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Kent" title="Sandwich, Kent">Sandwich</a>, Kent, which at the time employed 2,400 people.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> However, as of 2014, Pfizer has a reduced presence at the site;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> it also has a UK research unit in <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>On September 4, 2012, the FDA approved a Pfizer pill for a rare type of <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">leukemia</a>. The medicine, called Bosulif, treats <a href="/wiki/Chronic_myelogenous_leukemia" title="Chronic myelogenous leukemia">chronic myelogenous leukemia</a> (CML), a blood and <a href="/wiki/Bone_marrow" title="Bone marrow">bone marrow</a> disease that usually affects older adults.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2014, the company announced it would acquire Innopharma for $225 million, plus up to $135 million in milestone payments, in a deal that expanded Pfizer's range of generic and injectable drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p><p>On January 5, 2015, the company announced it would acquire a controlling interest in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Redvax&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Redvax (page does not exist)">Redvax</a> for an undisclosed sum. This deal expanded the company's vaccine portfolio targeting human <a href="/wiki/Cytomegalovirus" title="Cytomegalovirus">cytomegalovirus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In March 2015, the company announced it would restart its collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Eli_Lilly_and_Company" title="Eli Lilly and Company">Eli Lilly</a> surrounding the phase III trial of <a href="/wiki/Tanezumab" title="Tanezumab">Tanezumab</a>. Pfizer is expected to receive an upfront sum of $200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In June 2015, the company acquired two <a href="/wiki/Meningitis" title="Meningitis">meningitis</a> drugs from <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>—Nimenrix and <a href="/wiki/Mencevax" class="mw-redirect" title="Mencevax">Mencevax</a>—for around $130 million, expanding the company's <a href="/wiki/Meningococcal_disease" title="Meningococcal disease">meningococcal disease</a> portfolio of drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2016, the company announced it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Anacor_Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Anacor Pharmaceuticals">Anacor Pharmaceuticals</a> for $5.2 billion, expanding the companies portfolio in both inflammation and immunology drugs areas.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> On their final trading day, Anacor shares traded for $99.20 each, giving Anacor a market capitalisation of $4.5 billion. In August, the company made a $40 million bid for the assets of the now bankrupt <a href="/w/index.php?title=BIND_Therapeutics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="BIND Therapeutics (page does not exist)">BIND Therapeutics</a> through the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bankruptcy_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Bankruptcy Court">U.S. Bankruptcy Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The same month, the company announced it would acquire <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bamboo_Therapeutics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bamboo Therapeutics (page does not exist)">Bamboo Therapeutics</a> for $645 million, expanding the company's gene therapy offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Later, in August, the company announced the acquisition of cancer drug-maker -  <a href="/wiki/Medivation" title="Medivation">Medivation</a> - for $14 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> On Medivation's final day of trading, its shares were valued at $81.44 each, giving an effective market capitalisation of $13.52 billion. Two days later, Pfizer announced it would acquire <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZenecas</a> small-molecule antibiotics business for $1.575 billion<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> merging it into its <i>Essential Medicines</i> business<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In the same month the company licensed the anti-<a href="/wiki/CTLA4" class="mw-redirect" title="CTLA4">CTLA4</a> monoclonal antibody, ONC-392, from <a href="/w/index.php?title=OncoImmune&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="OncoImmune (page does not exist)">OncoImmune</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2019 the company announced it would acquire <a href="/w/index.php?title=Therachon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Therachon (page does not exist)">Therachon</a> for $810 million, expanding its rare disease portfolio through Theracons recombinant human fibroblast growth factor receptor 3 compound, aimed at treating conditions such as <a href="/wiki/Achondroplasia" title="Achondroplasia">achondroplasia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In June, Pfizer announced it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Array_Biopharma" class="mw-redirect" title="Array Biopharma">Array Biopharma</a> for $10.6 billion boosting its oncology pipeline.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoetis">Zoetis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Zoetis" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Zoetis" title="Zoetis">Zoetis</a></div>
<p>Plans to <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spin out</a> Zoetis, the Agriculture Division of Pfizer and later Pfizer Animal Health, were announced in 2012. Pfizer filed for registration of a Class A stock with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> on August 13, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Zoetis's <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">IPO</a> on February 1, 2013, sold 86.1 million shares for <a href="/wiki/US%24" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>2.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTIPO_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIPO-57">[57]</a></sup> Pfizer retained 414 million Class B shares, giving it an 83% controlling stake in the firm.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJIPO_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJIPO-58">[58]</a></sup> The offering's lead <a href="/wiki/Underwriters" class="mw-redirect" title="Underwriters">underwriters</a> were <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" class="mw-redirect" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTIPO_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIPO-57">[57]</a></sup> Most of the money raised through the IPO was used to pay off existing Pfizer debt.<sup id="cite_ref-CBSIPO_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBSIPO-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Attempted_AstraZeneca_acquisition">Attempted AstraZeneca acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Attempted AstraZeneca acquisition" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In April 2014, it was reported that Pfizer had reignited a $100 billion takeover bid for the UK-based <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> sparking political controversy in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> as well as in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On May 19, 2014, a "final offer" of £55 a share was rejected by the AstraZeneca board, which said the bid was too low and imposed too many risks. If successful, the takeover—the biggest in British history—would have made Pfizer the world's largest drug company.<sup id="cite_ref-PfizerBid_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PfizerBid-64">[64]</a></sup> Hopes for a renewed bid later in the year were dashed when Pfizer signed a major cancer drug deal with <a href="/wiki/Merck_KGaA" class="mw-redirect" title="Merck KGaA">Merck KGaA</a>, selling its sharing rights to develop an experimental <a href="/wiki/Immunotherapy" title="Immunotherapy">immunotherapy</a> drug for a fee of $850 million.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospira">Hospira</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hospira" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In February 2015, Pfizer and <a href="/wiki/Hospira" title="Hospira">Hospira</a> agreed that Pfizer would acquire Hospira for $15.2 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-66">[66]</a></sup> a deal in which Hospira shareholders would receive $90 in cash for each share they owned.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> News of the deal sent Hospira share prices up from $63.43 to $87.43 on a volume of 60.7 million shares.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Including debt, the deal is valued at around $17 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-66">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hospira" title="Hospira">Hospira</a> is the largest producer of generic injectable pharmaceuticals in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> On the final day of trading, Hospira shares traded for $89.96 each, giving a market capitalisation of $15.56 billion.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Attempted_Allergan_acquisition">Attempted Allergan acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Attempted Allergan acquisition" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Allergan" title="Allergan">Allergan</a></div>
<p>On November 23, 2015, Pfizer and <a href="/wiki/Allergan,_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Allergan, plc">Allergan, plc</a> announced their intention to merge for an approximate sum of $160 billion, making it the largest pharmaceutical deal ever, and the third largest corporate merger in history. As part of the deal, the Pfizer CEO, Ian Read, was to remain as CEO and chairman of the new company, to be called "Pfizer plc", with Allergan's CEO, Brent Saunders, becoming president and chief operating officer. As part of the deal, Allergan shareholders would receive 11.3 shares of the company, with Pfizer shareholders receiving one. The terms proposed that the merged company would maintain Allergan's <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Irish</a> domicile, resulting in the new company being subject to <a href="/wiki/Corporation_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporation tax">corporation tax</a> at the Irish rate of 12.5%--considerably lower than the 35% rate that Pfizer paid at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23_nov_2015_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_23_nov_2015-71">[71]</a></sup> The deal was to constitute a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Reverse merger">reverse merger</a>, whereby Allergan acquired Pfizer, with the new company then changing its name to "Pfizer, plc".<sup id="cite_ref-Genegnews_2015_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genegnews_2015-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_22_Nov_2015_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg_22_Nov_2015-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-premier_2015_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-premier_2015-74">[74]</a></sup> The deal was expected to be completed in the second half of 2016, subject to certain conditions: US and EU approval, approval from both sets of shareholders, and the completion of Allergan's divestiture of its generics division to <a href="/wiki/Teva_Pharmaceuticals" title="Teva Pharmaceuticals">Teva Pharmaceuticals</a> (expected in the first quarter of 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-Genegnews_2015_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genegnews_2015-72">[72]</a></sup> On April 6, 2016, Pfizer and Allergan announced they would be calling off the merger after the Obama administration introduced new laws intended to limit <a href="/wiki/Corporate_inversion" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate inversion">corporate tax inversions</a> (the extent to which companies could move their headquarters overseas in order to reduce the amount of taxes they pay).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pfizer_re-organisation">Pfizer re-organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pfizer re-organisation" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2018 Pfizer announced it would reorganise its business into three separate units; a higher-margin innovative medicines division, a lower-margin, off-patent drug division, and a consumer healthcare division, with a view to focussing on higher margin therapies.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pfizer_Consumer_Healthcare">Pfizer Consumer Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pfizer Consumer Healthcare" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In October 2017, reports emerged that Pfizer were undertaking a strategic review of their Consumer Healthcare division, with possible results ranging from a partial or complete spin-off or a direct sale<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> with the divestment expected to raise in the region of $15 billion for one of the largest Over-the-Counter businesses in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reckitt_Benckiser" title="Reckitt Benckiser">Reckitt Benckiser</a> expressed interest in bidding for the division earlier in October<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Sanofi" title="Sanofi">Sanofi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a> also being linked with bids for the business.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On March 22, Reckitt Benckiser pulled out of the deal, a day later GlaxoSmithKline also pulled out.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2018, <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a> announced that it, along with Pfizer, had reached an agreement to merge and combine their consumer healthcare divisions into a single entity. The combined entity would have sales of around £9.8 billon ($12.7 billion), with GSK maintaining a 68% controlling stake in the joint venture. Pfizer would own the remaining 32% shareholding. The deal builds on an earlier 2018 deal where GSK bought out Novartis' stake in the GSK-Novartis consumer healthcare joint business.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pfizer_off-patent_drug_business">Pfizer off-patent drug business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pfizer off-patent drug business" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In late July 2019, the company announced that it would spin off and merge its off-patent medicine division, Upjohn, with <a href="/wiki/Mylan" title="Mylan">Mylan</a>, forming a brand new pharmaceutical business with sales of around $20 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The new combined business will have a portfolio of drugs and brands including the <a href="/wiki/Epi-Pen" class="mw-redirect" title="Epi-Pen">Epi-Pen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viagra" class="mw-redirect" title="Viagra">Viagra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lipitor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lipitor">Lipitor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celebrex" class="mw-redirect" title="Celebrex">Celebrex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>The deal will be structured as an all-stock, Reverse Morris Trust transaction:
</p>
<ul><li>Upjohn will be spun off to Pfizer shareholders and then combined with Mylan</li>
<li>Each share of Mylan's stock will be converted into one share of the new company</li>
<li>Pfizer shareholders would own 57% of the combined new company and Mylan shareholders will own 43%</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_history">Acquisition history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acquisition history" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:1px #aaa solid;"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:center;;">Pfizer Acquisitions</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">
