</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg/170px-Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg/170px-Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shinjuku_Bunka_Quint_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of Pfizer Japan in Tokyo</div></div></div>
<p>Pfizer is organised into nine principal operating divisions: Primary Care, Specialty Care, Oncology, Emerging Markets, Established Products, Consumer Healthcare, Nutrition, Animal Health, and Capsugel.<sup id="cite_ref-leadstruc_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadstruc-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Partnerships" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In May 2015, Pfizer and a <a href="/wiki/Bar-Ilan_University" title="Bar-Ilan University">Bar-Ilan University</a> laboratory announced a partnership based on the development of medical <a href="/wiki/DNA_nanotechnology" title="DNA nanotechnology">DNA nanotechnology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research and development" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Pfizer's research and development activities are organised into two principal groups: the PharmaTherapeutics Research &amp; Development Group, which focuses on the discovery of small molecules and related modalities; and the BioTherapeutics Research &amp; Development Group, which focuses on large-molecule research, including vaccines.<sup id="cite_ref-leadstruc_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadstruc-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2007, Pfizer invested $8.1 billion in research and development, the largest R&amp;D investment in the pharmaceutical industry.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>Pfizer has R&amp;D facilities in the following locations:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pearl_River,_New_York" title="Pearl River, New York">Pearl River, New York</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Groton,_Connecticut" title="Groton, Connecticut">Groton, Connecticut</a> (Largest R&amp;D site)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andover,_Massachusetts" title="Andover, Massachusetts">Andover, Massachusetts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/La_Jolla,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="La Jolla, California">La Jolla, California</a> (around 1,000 staff, focused on cancer drugs);<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_San_Francisco,_California" title="South San Francisco, California">South San Francisco</a>, California</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge</a>, Massachusetts</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a>, Missouri</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sandwich,_Kent" title="Sandwich, Kent">Sandwich</a>, United Kingdom</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, United Kingdom.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morrisville,_North_Carolina" title="Morrisville, North Carolina">Morrisville</a>, North Carolina</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, India</li></ul><p>In 2007, Pfizer announced plans to close or sell the Loughbeg API facility, located at Loughbeg, <a href="/wiki/Ringaskiddy" title="Ringaskiddy">Ringaskiddy</a>, Cork, Ireland by mid to end of 2008. In 2007, Pfizer announced plans to completely close the Ann Arbor, Nagoya and Amboise Research facilities by the end of 2008, eliminating 2,160 jobs and idling the $300 million Michigan facility, which in recent years had seen expansion worth millions of dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p><p>On June 18, 2007, Pfizer announced it would move the Animal Health Research (VMRD) division based in Sandwich, England, to Kalamazoo, Michigan.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On February 1, 2011, Pfizer announced the closure of the Research and Development centre in Sandwich, with the loss of 2,400 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Pfizer subsequently announced it would be maintaining a significant presence at Sandwich, with around 650 staff continuing to be based at the site.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>On September 1, 2011, Pfizer announced it had agreed to a 10-year lease of more than 180,000 square feet of research space from <a href="/wiki/MIT" class="mw-redirect" title="MIT">MIT</a> in a building to be constructed just north of the MIT campus in Cambridge, Massachusetts. The space will house Pfizer's Cardiovascular, Metabolic and Endocrine Disease Research Unit and its Neuroscience Research Unit; Pfizer anticipated moving into the space once it was completed in late 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2013, products in Pfizer's development pipeline included <a href="/wiki/Dimebon" class="mw-redirect" title="Dimebon">dimebon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanezumab" title="Tanezumab">tanezumab</a>.
</p><p>In 2018, Pfizer announced that it would end its work on research into treatments for <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's disease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parkinsonism" title="Parkinsonism">Parkinsonism</a> (a symptom of <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease">Parkinson's disease</a> and other conditions).  The company stated that approximately 300 researchers would lose their jobs as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-Hiltzik_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hiltzik-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Products" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>As of 2017, Pfizer split its business into two primary segments: (1) innovative health, which includes branded drugs and vaccines, and (2) essential health. In 2016, innovative health generated $29.2 billion in revenue and essential health generated $23.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Patented_pharmaceuticals">Patented pharmaceuticals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Patented pharmaceuticals" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="United States incidence of invasive pneumococcal disease before and after introduction of the 7-valent and 13-valent pneumococcal vaccines." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg/220px-US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="752" data-file-height="452"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 132px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg/220px-US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg" data-alt="United States incidence of invasive pneumococcal disease before and after introduction of the 7-valent and 13-valent pneumococcal vaccines." data-width="220" data-height="132" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_incidence_of_invasive_streptococcal_disease_before_and_after_vaccine_introduction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>United States incidence of invasive pneumococcal disease before and after introduction of the 7-valent and 13-valent pneumococcal vaccines.<sup id="cite_ref-cdc.gov_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdc.gov-99">[99]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Key current and Pfizer products include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Prevnar" class="mw-redirect" title="Prevnar">Prevnar</a> (13-valent conjugate pneumococcal vaccine) is a vaccine for the prevention of invasive pneumococcal infections. The introduction of the original, 7-valent version of the vaccine in 1999 led to a 75% reduction in the incidence of invasive pneumococcal infections among children under age 5 in the United States. An improved version of the vaccine, providing coverage of 13 bacterial variants, was introduced in early 2010, and granted a patent in India in 2017. As of 2012 the rate of invasive infections among children under age 5 has been reduced by an additional 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-cdc.gov_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdc.gov-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyrica">Lyrica</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pregabalin" title="Pregabalin">pregabalin</a>) for <a href="/wiki/Neuropathic_pain" title="Neuropathic pain">neuropathic pain</a>. Sales of Lyrica were $4.6 billion in 2013; the US patent on Lyrica was challenged by generic manufacturers and was upheld in 2014, giving Pfizer exclusivity for Lyrica in the US until 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li>Xeljanz (<a href="/wiki/Tofacitinib" title="Tofacitinib">tofacitinib</a>) for rheumatoid arthritis and ulcerative colitis, which had sales of $1.77 billion in 2018 and in January 2019 it was top drug in the United States for <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-consumer_advertising" title="Direct-to-consumer advertising">direct-to-consumer advertising</a>, passing <a href="/wiki/Adalimumab" title="Adalimumab">Humira</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li></ul><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoloft_bottles.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Zoloft_bottles.jpg/220px-Zoloft_bottles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1223" data-file-height="1088"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 196px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Zoloft_bottles.jpg/220px-Zoloft_bottles.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="196" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zoloft_bottles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bottles of the antidepressant Zoloft</div></div></div>
<ul><li class="mw-empty-elt"></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Generics">Generics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Generics" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Xanax_2_mg.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Xanax_2_mg.jpg/170px-Xanax_2_mg.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="997" data-file-height="1477"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 252px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Xanax_2_mg.jpg/170px-Xanax_2_mg.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="252" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Xanax_2_mg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Xanax (alprazolam) 2 mg tri-score tablets</div></div></div>
<p>In addition to marketing branded pharmaceuticals, Pfizer is involved in the manufacture and sale of <a href="/wiki/Generic_drug" title="Generic drug">generics</a>. In the US it does this through its Greenstone subsidiary, which it acquired as part of the acquisition of Pharmacia.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Pfizer also has a licensing deal in place with <a href="/wiki/Aurobindo_Pharma" title="Aurobindo Pharma">Aurobindo</a>, which grants the former access to a variety of oral solid generic products.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> 
Key historical generics include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atorvastatin" title="Atorvastatin">Atorvastatin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Drug_nomenclature#Publication_policies_for_nonproprietary_and_proprietary_names" title="Drug nomenclature">trade name</a> Lipitor), a <a href="/wiki/Statin" title="Statin">statin</a> for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Hypercholesterolemia" title="Hypercholesterolemia">hypercholesterolemia</a>. Lipitor was developed by Pfizer legacy company Parke-Davis, a subsidiary of Warner-Lambert and first marketed in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-FDA_Lipitor_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FDA_Lipitor-104">[104]</a></sup> Although atorvastatin was the fifth drug in the class of <a href="/wiki/Statins" class="mw-redirect" title="Statins">statins</a> to be developed, clinical trials showed that atorvastatin caused a more dramatic reduction in <a href="/wiki/LDL-C" class="mw-redirect" title="LDL-C">LDL-C</a> than the other statin drugs. From 1996 to 2012 under the trade name Lipitor, atorvastatin became the world's best-selling drug of all time, with more than $125 billion in sales over approximately 14.5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-url_Crain_2011_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-url_Crain_2011-105">[105]</a></sup> Lipitor alone "provided up to a quarter of Pfizer Inc.'s annual revenue for years."<sup id="cite_ref-url_Crain_2011_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-url_Crain_2011-105">[105]</a></sup> The patent expired in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_Wire_Staff_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Wire_Staff-106">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diflucan" class="mw-redirect" title="Diflucan">Diflucan</a> (fluconazole), the first orally available treatment for severe fungal infections. Fluconazole is recommended as a first-line treatment in <a href="/wiki/Invasive_candidiasis" title="Invasive candidiasis">invasive candidiasis</a><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and is widely used in the prophylaxis of severe fungal infections in premature infants.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Fluconazole is on the World Health Organization's List of Essential Medicines.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-109">[109]</a></sup> Patent protection ended in 2004 and 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flagyl" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagyl">Flagyl</a> (metronidazole) is a <a href="/wiki/Nitroimidazole" title="Nitroimidazole">nitroimidazole</a> <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotic</a> medication used particularly for <a href="/wiki/Anaerobe" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaerobe">anaerobic</a> <a href="/wiki/Bacterium" class="mw-redirect" title="Bacterium">bacteria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protozoa" title="Protozoa">protozoa</a>. It is <a href="/wiki/Antibacterial" class="mw-redirect" title="Antibacterial">antibacterial</a> against <a href="/wiki/Anaerobic_organisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaerobic organisms">anaerobic organisms</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Amoebicide" class="mw-redirect" title="Amoebicide">amoebicide</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Antiprotozoal" title="Antiprotozoal">antiprotozoal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-monograph_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-monograph-111">[111]</a></sup> As of 2018, it is second line for first episodes of mild-to-moderate <i><a href="/wiki/Clostridium_difficile_(bacteria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clostridium difficile (bacteria)">Clostridium difficile</a></i> infection (formerly was first-line).<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> It is on the World Health Organization's List of Essential Medicines.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-109">[109]</a></sup> The original patent protection ended in 1982, but reformulation <a href="/wiki/Evergreening" title="Evergreening">evergreening</a> occurred thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norvasc" class="mw-redirect" title="Norvasc">Norvasc</a> (amlodipine), an <a href="/wiki/Antihypertensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Antihypertensive">antihypertensive</a> drug of the dihydropyridine calcium channel blocker class. Amlodipine is on the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization%27s_List_of_Essential_Medicines" class="mw-redirect" title="World Health Organization's List of Essential Medicines">World Health Organization's List of Essential Medicines</a>, a list of the most important medication needed in a basic <a href="/wiki/Health_system" title="Health system">health system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-109">[109]</a></sup> Patent protection ended in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zithromax" class="mw-redirect" title="Zithromax">Zithromax</a> (azithromycin), a macrolide antibiotic that is recommended by the Infectious Disease Society of America as a first line treatment for certain cases of community-acquired pneumonia.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Patent protection ended in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zoloft" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoloft">Zoloft</a> (sertraline), is an <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressant</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitor" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor">selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor</a> (SSRI) class. It was introduced to the market by Pfizer in 1991. Sertraline is primarily prescribed for <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a> in adult <a href="/wiki/Outpatients" class="mw-redirect" title="Outpatients">outpatients</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Obsessive-compulsive_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Obsessive-compulsive disorder">obsessive–compulsive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_anxiety_disorder" title="Social anxiety disorder">social anxiety</a> disorders in both adults and children. In 2011, it was the second-most prescribed antidepressant on the U.S. retail market, with 37 million prescriptions.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The patent expired 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_practices">Promotional practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Promotional practices" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_pharmaceutical_settlements" title="List of largest pharmaceutical settlements">List of largest pharmaceutical settlements</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_v._Parke-Davis" title="Franklin v. Parke-Davis">Franklin v. Parke-Davis</a></div>
<p>Pfizer has long been known within the industry as one of the more aggressive marketers of their products.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Access to Wyeth internal documents has revealed <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_marketing" title="Pharmaceutical marketing">marketing</a> strategies used to promote <a href="/wiki/Neurontin" class="mw-redirect" title="Neurontin">Neurontin</a> for <a href="/wiki/Off-label_use" title="Off-label use">off-label use</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Food and Drug Administration (United States)">U.S. Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) approved <a href="/wiki/Gabapentin" title="Gabapentin">gabapentin</a> (Neurontin, Pfizer) only for treatment of <a href="/wiki/Seizures" class="mw-redirect" title="Seizures">seizures</a>. <a href="/wiki/Warner%E2%80%93Lambert" title="Warner–Lambert">Warner–Lambert</a>, which merged with Pfizer in 2000, used activities not usually associated with sales promotion, including <a href="/wiki/Continuing_medical_education" title="Continuing medical education">continuing medical education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">research</a>, sponsored articles about the drug for the medical literature, and alleged suppression of unfavorable study results, to promote gabapentin. Within 5 years the drug was being widely used for the <a href="/wiki/Off-label" class="mw-redirect" title="Off-label">off-label</a> treatment of pain and psychiatric conditions. Warner–Lambert admitted to charges that it violated FDA regulations by <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-label_promotion_pharmaceutical_settlements" title="List of off-label promotion pharmaceutical settlements">promoting the drug</a> for pain, psychiatric conditions, migraine, and other unapproved uses, and paid <a href="/wiki/List_of_Largest_Pharmaceutical_Settlements" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Largest Pharmaceutical Settlements">$430 million</a> to resolve criminal and civil health care liability charges.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> A recent Cochrane review concluded that gabapentin is ineffective in migraine prophylaxis.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The American Academy of Neurology rates it as having unproven efficacy, while the Canadian Headache Society and the European Federation of Neurological Societies rate its use as being supported by moderate and low-quality evidence, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2009, Pfizer agreed to pay <a href="/wiki/List_of_Largest_Pharmaceutical_Settlements" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Largest Pharmaceutical Settlements">$2.3 billion</a> to settle civil and criminal allegations that it had illegally marketed four drugs—<a href="/wiki/Bextra" class="mw-redirect" title="Bextra">Bextra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geodon" class="mw-redirect" title="Geodon">Geodon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zyvox" class="mw-redirect" title="Zyvox">Zyvox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyrica">Lyrica</a>—for non-approved uses; it was Pfizer's fourth such settlement in a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-2.3_nytimes_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2.3_nytimes-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wapo_offlabel_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo_offlabel-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pfizer_agrees_record_fraud_fine_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pfizer_agrees_record_fraud_fine-129">[129]</a></sup> The payment included $1.3 billion in criminal penalties for felony violations of the Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act, and $1 billion to settle allegations it had illegally promoted the drugs for uses that were not approved by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Food and Drug Administration (United States)">U.S. Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) and caused <a href="/wiki/False_Claims_Act" title="False Claims Act">false claims</a> to be submitted to Federal and State programs. The criminal fine was the largest ever assessed in the United States up to that time.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Pfizer has entered an extensive <a href="/wiki/Corporate_integrity_agreement" title="Corporate integrity agreement">corporate integrity agreement</a> with the Office of Inspector General and will be required to make substantial structural reforms within the company, and maintain the Pfizer website (www.pfizer.com/pmc) to track the company's post marketing commitments. Pfizer had to also put a searchable database of all payments to physicians the company had made on the Pfizer website by March 31, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p><p>Peter Rost was vice president in charge of the endocrinology division at Pharmacia before and during its acquisition by Pfizer. During that time he raised concerns internally about <a href="/wiki/Kickback_(bribery)" title="Kickback (bribery)">kickbacks</a> and off-label marketing of Genotropin, Pharmacia's <a href="/wiki/Human_growth_hormone" class="mw-redirect" title="Human growth hormone">human growth hormone</a> drug. Pfizer reported the Pharmacia marketing practices to the FDA and Department of Justice; Rost was unaware of this and filed an FCA lawsuit against Pfizer. Pfizer kept him on, but isolated him until the FCA suit was unsealed in 2005. The Justice Department declined to intervene, and Pfizer fired him, and he filed a wrongful termination suit against Pfizer.<sup id="cite_ref-Edwards_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edwards-132">[132]</a></sup> Pfizer won a summary dismissal of the case, with the court ruling that the evidence showed Pfizer had decided to fire Rost prior to learning of his whistleblower activities.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>A "whistleblower suit" was filed in 2005 against <a href="/wiki/Wyeth" title="Wyeth">Wyeth</a>, which was acquired by Pfizer in 2009, alleging that the company illegally marketed their drug <a href="/wiki/Rapamune" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapamune">Rapamune</a>. Wyeth is targeted in the suit for off-label marketing, targeting specific doctors and medical facilities to increase sales of Rapamune, trying to get current transplant patients to change from their current transplant drugs to Rapamune and for specifically targeting African-Americans. According to the whistleblowers, Wyeth also provided doctors and hospitals with kickbacks to prescribe the drug in the form of grants, donations and other money.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> In 2013, the company pleaded guilty to criminal mis-branding violations under the Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act. By August 2014 it had paid $491 million in civil and criminal penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Magazine" title="Harper's Magazine">Harper's Magazine</a></i> publisher <a href="/wiki/John_R._MacArthur" title="John R. MacArthur">John MacArthur</a>, Pfizer withdrew "between $400,000 and a million dollars" worth of ads from their magazine following an unflattering article on depression medication.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>Pfizer is party to a number of lawsuits stemming from its pharmaceutical products as well as the practices of various companies it has merged with or acquired.<sup id="cite_ref-2.3_nytimes_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2.3_nytimes-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wapo_offlabel_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo_offlabel-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pfizer_agrees_record_fraud_fine_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pfizer_agrees_record_fraud_fine-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Quigley_Co.">Quigley Co.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Quigley Co." data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Pfizer acquired Quigley in 1968, and the division sold <a href="/wiki/Asbestos" title="Asbestos">asbestos</a>-containing insulation products until the early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Asbestos victims and Pfizer have been negotiating a settlement deal that calls for Pfizer to pay $430 million to 80 percent of existing plaintiffs. It will also place an additional $535 million into an asbestos settlement trust that will compensate future plaintiffs as well as the remaining 20 percent of current plaintiffs with claims against Pfizer and Quigley. The compensation deal is worth $965 million all up. Of that $535 million, $405 million is in a 40-year note from Pfizer, while $100 million will come from insurance policies.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Bjork.E2.80.93Shiley_heart_valve"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bjork–Shiley_heart_valve">Bjork–Shiley heart valve</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bjork–Shiley heart valve" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Pfizer purchased Shiley in 1979 at the onset of its Convexo-Concave valve ordeal, involving the <a href="/wiki/Bjork%E2%80%93Shiley_valve" class="mw-redirect" title="Bjork–Shiley valve">Bjork–Shiley heart valve</a>. Approximately 500 people died when defective valves failed and, in 1994, the United States ruled against Pfizer for ~$200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Abdullahi_v._Pfizer.2C_Inc_and_Trovafloxacin_.28Trovan.29_Controversy."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Abdullahi_v._Pfizer,_Inc_and_Trovafloxacin_(Trovan)_Controversy."><i>Abdullahi v. Pfizer, Inc and Trovafloxacin (Trovan) Controversy.</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Abdullahi v. Pfizer, Inc and Trovafloxacin (Trovan) Controversy." data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abdullahi_v._Pfizer,_Inc." title="Abdullahi v. Pfizer, Inc.">Abdullahi v. Pfizer, Inc.</a></div>
<p>In 1996, an outbreak of measles, cholera, and bacterial meningitis occurred in Nigeria. Pfizer representatives and personnel from a contract research organization (CRO) traveled to Kano, Nigeria to set up a clinical trial and administer an experimental <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trovafloxacin" title="Trovafloxacin">trovafloxacin</a>, to approximately 200 children.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Local Kano officials report that more than 50 children died in the experiment, while many others developed mental and physical deformities.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The nature and frequency of both fatalities and other adverse outcomes were similar to those historically found among pediatric patients treated for meningitis in sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In 2001, families of the children, as well as the governments of Kano and Nigeria, filed lawsuits regarding the treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> According to the news program <i><a href="/wiki/Democracy_Now!" title="Democracy Now!">Democracy Now!</a></i>, "[r]esearchers did not obtain signed consent forms, and medical personnel said Pfizer did not tell parents their children were getting the experimental drug."<sup id="cite_ref-DN_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN-146">[146]</a></sup> The lawsuits also accuse Pfizer of using the outbreak to perform unapproved human testing, as well as allegedly under-dosing a control group being treated with traditional antibiotics in order to skew the results of the trial in favor of Trovan. While the specific facts of the case remain in dispute, both Nigerian medical personnel and at least one Pfizer physician have stated that the trial was conducted without regulatory approval.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>In 2007, Pfizer published a Statement of Defense letter.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The letter states that the drug's oral form was safer and easier to administer, that Trovan had been used safely in over 5000 Americans prior to the Nigerian trial, that mortality in the patients treated by Pfizer was lower than that observed historically in African meningitis epidemics, and that no unusual side effects, unrelated to meningitis, were observed after 4 weeks.
</p><p>In June 2010, the US Supreme Court rejected Pfizer's appeal against a ruling allowing lawsuits by the Nigerian families to proceed.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2010, <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> released <a href="/wiki/United_States_diplomatic_cables_leak" title="United States diplomatic cables leak">US diplomatic cables</a>, which indicate that Pfizer had hired investigators to find evidence of corruption against Nigerian attorney general Aondoakaa to persuade him to drop legal action.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> reporter Joe Stephens, who helped break the story in 2000, called these actions "dangerously close to blackmail."<sup id="cite_ref-DN_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN-146">[146]</a></sup> In response, the company has released a press statement describing the allegations as "preposterous" and stating that they acted in good faith.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Aondoakka, who had allegedly demanded bribes from Pfizer in return for a settlement of the case,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> was declared unfit for office and had his U.S. visa revoked in association with corruption charges in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Retrovirus_lawsuit">Retrovirus lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Retrovirus lawsuit" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>A scientist claims she was infected by a genetically modified virus while working for Pfizer. In her federal lawsuit she says she has been intermittently paralyzed by the Pfizer-designed virus. "McClain, of Deep River, suspects she was inadvertently exposed, through work by a former Pfizer colleague in 2002 or 2003, to an engineered form of the <a href="/wiki/Lentivirus" title="Lentivirus">lentivirus</a>, a virus similar to the one that can lead to acquired immune deficiency syndrome, also known as AIDS."<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The court found that McClain failed to demonstrate that her illness was caused by exposure to the lentivirus,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> but also that Pfizer violated whistleblower laws.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Blue_Cross_Blue_Shield">Blue Cross Blue Shield</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Blue Cross Blue Shield" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Health insurance company <a href="/wiki/Blue_Cross_Blue_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue Cross Blue Shield">Blue Cross Blue Shield</a> (BCBS) filed a lawsuit against Pfizer for reportedly illegally marketing their drugs <a href="/wiki/Bextra" class="mw-redirect" title="Bextra">Bextra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geodon" class="mw-redirect" title="Geodon">Geodon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyrica">Lyrica</a>. BCBS is reporting that Pfizer used "kickbacks" and wrongly persuaded doctors to prescribe the drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> FiercePharma reported that "According to the suit, the drugmaker not only handed out those "misleading" materials on off-label uses, but sent doctors on Caribbean junkets and paid them $2,000 honoraria in return for their listening to lectures about Bextra. More than 5,000 healthcare professionals were entertained at meetings in Bahamas, Virgin Islands, and across the U.S., the suit alleges."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The case was settled in 2014 for $325M.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brigham_Young_University">Brigham Young University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Brigham Young University" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Controversy arose over the drug "Celebrex". <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">Brigham Young University</a> (BYU) said that a professor of chemistry, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_L._Simmons" title="Daniel L. Simmons">Daniel L. Simmons</a>, discovered an enzyme in the 1990s that would later lead towards the development of Celebrex. BYU was originally seeking 15% royalty on sales, which would equate to $9.7 billion. The court filings show that a research agreement was made with <a href="/wiki/Monsanto" title="Monsanto">Monsanto</a>, whose pharmaceutical business was later acquired by Pfizer, to develop a better aspirin. The enzyme that Dr. Simmons claims to have discovered would induce pain and inflammation while causing gastrointestinal problems, which Celebrex is used to reduce those issues. A battle ensued, lasting over six years, because BYU claimed that Pfizer did not give him credit or compensation while Pfizer claims it had met all obligations regarding the Monsanto agreement. This culminated in a $450 million amicable settlement without going to trial. Pfizer said it would take a $450 million charge against first quarter earnings to settle.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation_in_which_Pfizer_was_not_a_party">Litigation in which Pfizer was not a party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Litigation in which Pfizer was not a party" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Pfizer was discussed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Kelo_v._New_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelo v. New London">Kelo v. New London</a> case that was decided by <a href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Supreme Court">U.S. Supreme Court</a> in 2005.  In February 1998 Pfizer announced it would build a research facility in  <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London</a>, Connecticut, and local planners, hoping to promote <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> and build on the influx of jobs the planned facility would bring to the town, created a plan that included seizing property to redevelop it under <a href="/wiki/Eminent_domain" title="Eminent domain">eminent domain</a>, and local residents sued to stop the seizure.  The case went to the Supreme Court, and with regard to Pfizer, the court cited a prior decision that said: "The record clearly demonstrates that the development plan was not intended to serve the interests of Pfizer, Inc., or any other private entity, but rather, to revitalize the local economy by creating temporary and permanent jobs, generating a significant increase in tax revenue, encouraging spin-off economic activities and maximizing public access to the waterfront”.<sup id="cite_ref-Kelo_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kelo-165">[165]</a></sup>   The Supreme Court allowed the eminent domain to proceed.<sup id="cite_ref-Kelo_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kelo-165">[165]</a></sup>  Pfizer opened the facility in 2001 but abandoned it in 2009, angering residents of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>Between 2002 and 2008, Pfizer reduced its greenhouse emissions by 20%,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> and committed to reducing emissions by an additional 20% by 2012. In 2012 the company was named to the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Disclosure_Project" title="Carbon Disclosure Project">Carbon Disclosure Project</a>'s Carbon Leadership Index in recognition of its efforts to reduce greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p><p>Pfizer has inherited Wyeth's liabilities in the <a href="/wiki/American_Cyanamid" title="American Cyanamid">American Cyanamid</a> site in Bridgewater, New Jersey. This site is highly toxic and an EPA declared Superfund site. Pfizer has since attempted to remediate this land in order to clean and develop it for future profits and potential public uses.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The Sierra Club and the Edison Wetlands Association have come out in opposition to the cleanup plan, arguing that the area is subject to flooding, which could cause pollutants to leach. The EPA considers the plan the most reasonable from considerations of safety and cost-effectiveness, arguing that an alternative plan involving trucking contaminated soil off site could expose cleanup workers. The EPA's position is backed by the environmental watchdog group CRISIS.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2002, a chemical explosion at the Groton plant injured seven people and caused the evacuation of over 100 homes in the surrounding area.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_lobbying">Political lobbying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Political lobbying" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>Pfizer is a leading member of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Global_Leadership_Coalition" title="U.S. Global Leadership Coalition">U.S. Global Leadership Coalition</a>, a Washington D.C.-based coalition of over 400 major companies and NGOs that advocates for a larger International Affairs Budget, which funds American diplomatic, humanitarian, and development efforts abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p><p>Pfizer is one of the single largest lobbying interests in United States politics. For example, in the first 9 months of 2009 Pfizer spent over $16.3 million on lobbying US congressional lawmakers, making them the sixth largest lobbying interest in the US (following Pharmaceutical Research and Manufacturers of America (PhRMA), which ranked fourth but also represents many of their interests). A spokeswoman for Pfizer said the company “wanted to make sure our voice is heard in this conversation” in regards to the company's expenditure of $25 million in 2010 to lobby health care reform.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> cables released by the <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">whistleblower</a> site <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a>, Pfizer "lobbied against New Zealand getting a <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> agreement with the United States because it objected to New Zealand's restrictive drug buying rules and tried to get rid of New Zealand's former health minister, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Clark" title="Helen Clark">Helen Clark</a>, in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-NZ_Herald_10695239_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NZ_Herald_10695239-174">[174]</a></sup></p><p>In an example of the <a href="/wiki/Revolving_door_(politics)" title="Revolving door (politics)">revolving door between government and industry</a> in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Gottlieb" title="Scott Gottlieb">Scott Gotlieb</a>, who resigned as the <a href="/wiki/FDA_commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="FDA commissioner">US FDA Commissioner</a> in April 2019, joined the Pfizer <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> three months later, in July.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_and_diversity">Employment and diversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Employment and diversity" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p>Since 2004, Pfizer has received a 100% rating every year on the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Equality_Index" title="Corporate Equality Index">Corporate Equality Index</a>, released by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign Foundation</a>.
</p><p>In 2012, Pfizer's Canadian division, which then employed 2,890 people, was named one of <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Top_100_Employers#Montreal_Top_15_Winners" title="Canada's Top 100 Employers">Montreal's Top 15 Employers</a>, the only research-based pharmaceutical company to receive this honor.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Management" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Read" title="Ian Read">Ian Read</a> took over as CEO from <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Kindler" title="Jeff Kindler">Jeff Kindler</a>. In 2019, Ian Read left the CEO role and became executive chairman, with COO Albert Bouria taking the CEO role.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Involvement_in_developing_world_health_issues">Involvement in developing world health issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Involvement in developing world health issues" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<p>Pfizer makes the anti-fungal drug <a href="/wiki/Fluconazole" title="Fluconazole">fluconazole</a> available free of charge to governmental and <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> (NGOs) in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> with a greater than 1% prevalence of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_New_York_Times_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_New_York_Times-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The company has also pledged to provide up to 740 million doses of its anti-<a href="/wiki/Pneumococcal_infection" title="Pneumococcal infection">pneumococcal</a> vaccine at discounted rates to infants and young children in 41 developing countries in association with the <a href="/wiki/GAVI_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="GAVI Alliance">GAVI Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, Pfizer and the <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Gates Foundation</a> announced a joint effort to provide affordable access to Pfizer's long-lasting injectable contraceptive, <a href="/wiki/Depot_medroxyprogesterone_acetate" class="mw-redirect" title="Depot medroxyprogesterone acetate">medroxyprogesterone acetate</a>, to three million women in developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pfizer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">

<ul><li><span><noscript><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="19" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 32px;height: 19px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png" data-alt="flag" data-width="32" data-height="19" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/48px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_New_York_City.svg/64px-Flag_of_New_York_City.svg.png 2x" data-class="noviewer thumbborder"> </span></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:New_York_City" title="Portal:New York City">New York City portal</a></span></li>
<li><span><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/28px-Industry5.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 28px;height: 28px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/28px-Industry5.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="28" data-height="28" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/42px-Industry5.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/56px-Industry5.svg.png 2x" data-class="noviewer"> </span></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Companies" title="Portal:Companies">Companies portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
